<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f31caf85-be91-48eb-8e40-92d524742e65'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/494576-what-exactly-does-it-mean-by-psychic-does">What exactly does it mean by psychic? Does she communicate with the dead?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_494576'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F13466202-talented">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/494576-what-exactly-does-it-mean-by-psychic-does">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/494576-what-exactly-does-it-mean-by-psychic-does">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/12864262-carolyn-snow"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1347756870i/12864262._UX100_CR0,15,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/12864262-carolyn-snow">Carolyn Snow</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    No. She is what's called a Mind Manipulator, which is a type of psychic talent in the book. She also has telekinesis and some ability to alter the ele<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    No. She is what's called a Mind Manipulator, which is a type of psychic talent in the book. She also has telekinesis and some ability to alter the elements (in her case, weather).<br /><br />Mind Manipulation only works on the living. She can see inside people's heads, read their thoughts, and feel their emotions. She can forcibly break down the barriers most people set over their minds so she can't read them, but she only does this when she feels she has to, or is ordered to for an assignment. Because of this, she always knows when a person is telling the truth.<br /><br />She also has the ability to communicate telepathically, and when she's emotionally close to someone, or they have her talent or can mimic it, the other person can communicate telepathically with her as well. Those she is emotionally closest to also seem to be people she has a permanent psychic connection to - one of these people would later on die, and she felt their death in her emotions and mind, because she was truly connected to them.<br /><br />She doesn't have a lot of psychic powers that we are more acquainted with, though - she can't talk to spirits, commune with the dead, astrally project, see the future, etc. There is another, separate talent that allows the person to see the future, however. No talent allows anyone to communicate with dead people, or other spirits/ghosts/etc.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/845680002" />
    <a title="Jennifer (The Nightly Book Owl)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16802491-jennifer-the-nightly-book-owl"><img alt="Jennifer (The Nightly Book Owl)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392178807p2/16802491.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/845680002?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer (The Nightly Book Owl)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer (The Nightly Book Owl)" href="/user/show/16802491-jennifer-the-nightly-book-owl">Jennifer (The Nightly Book Owl)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16802491-jennifer-the-nightly-book-owl?shelf=mary-sue">mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16802491-jennifer-the-nightly-book-owl?shelf=forgettable">forgettable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16802491-jennifer-the-nightly-book-owl?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16802491-jennifer-the-nightly-book-owl?shelf=try-hard">try-hard</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16802491-jennifer-the-nightly-book-owl?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16802491-jennifer-the-nightly-book-owl?shelf=obviously-a-romance-in-disguise">obviously-a-romance-in-disguise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16802491-jennifer-the-nightly-book-owl?shelf=douchebag-alert">douchebag-alert</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer845680002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5904413507692570810">Actual rating: 1.5<br/><br/><b>I received a free copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. </b><br/><br/><a href='http://thenightlybookowl.wordpress.com/2014/02/08/book-review-talented-by-sophie-davis/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This review can also be read at The Nightly Book Owl.</a><br/><br/><i>TOXIC is an agency within the government that utilizes each child's unique ability in the most advantageous way. </i><br/><br/>I’m sorry. I thought I was supposed to be reading a book about a kickass assassin out for revenge against the man responsible for the death of her parents - not a soap opera. There was just so many things wrong with this novel and that’s with ign</span>
  <span id="freeText5904413507692570810" style="display:none">Actual rating: 1.5<br /><br /><b>I received a free copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. </b><br /><br /><a href="http://thenightlybookowl.wordpress.com/2014/02/08/book-review-talented-by-sophie-davis/" rel="nofollow noopener">This review can also be read at The Nightly Book Owl.</a><br /><br /><i>TOXIC is an agency within the government that utilizes each child's unique ability in the most advantageous way. </i><br /><br />I’m sorry. I thought I was supposed to be reading a book about a kickass assassin out for revenge against the man responsible for the death of her parents - not a soap opera. There was just so many things wrong with this novel and that’s with ignoring the blinding grammatical errors (on a side note, the book really needs a professional editor). <br /><br /><i>Telepathy was not uncommon but advanced Mind Manipulation, as I was capable of, was extremely rare.</i><br /><br /><i>I had felt different my whole life, mostly because I am different. </i><br /><br /><i>“..Your powers are so much stronger than any Talent I’ve ever met,” he sounded almost reverent when he said the last part. </i><br /><br />Hmm… unless I’m completely crazy, I’m pretty sure everyone is different, so um… what exactly does that even mean? I’m so tired of young adult novels where the main character is just so friggin special. Worse yet, when they just know that they’re so speshul and different. Talia is your typical mary sue. She’s just so special. I mean, she can move objects with her mind, read other people’s minds, project her feelings to other people with her mind. Oh and she can also manipulate people into doing what she wants… with her mind. This particular talent is extremely rare, and she’s just so special because of it. I can’t stress this enough, guys. She’s so special. Don’t question it. Just roll with it. <br /><br /><i>When had I become the kind of girl who played boys against each other? Let boys fight over her? </i><br /><br />Answer? Since the start of the book. Despite being utterly boring, Talia manages to make two hot guys fall instantly in love with her. When are these cheesy instalove love triangles ever going to stop? They just keep coming. I don’t even understand why these guys like Talia so much. She’s just so whiny and annoying, but I guess it makes sense ‘cause she’s a very speshul snowflake, and there’s just “something about her.” She’s fascinating, and these two boys just can’t get enough of her. Cue sexual tension. <br /><br /><i>The last thing I should be devoting energy to was boys.</i><br /><br />Proceed thinking about said boys further. Talia is an assassin. Supposedly, she’s in training to become one of the deadliest assassins. Riiiiight. I don’t even know what to say. Talia is constantly thinking about her love problems when clearly, she should really focus on, you know, not getting killed. I would think that takes top priority, but Talia obviously thinks otherwise. She has long curly hair that, ugh, just wouldn’t look good short. Nevermind that it is impractical in missions, flying all over her face and whatnot. A girl’s gotta look good, amirite? What’s really important here is that she looks damn good doing it. <br /><br />The whole thing was just drama after drama. This book was supposed to be about assassins. No. It is a poorly disguised romance novel with some extra elements thrown in there. He loves me, he loves me not. OMG I shouldn’t be thinking about Erik this way. I have Donovan, but I feel different around Erik. It’s intoxicating, but Donovan loves me. Do I love him? It just goes on and on. I just want some action. Is that too much to ask for in a book that is supposed to be centering on an assassin? <br /><br /><i>The first was a shiny, metal thermos that he warmed in the fire. The next contained bright red raspberries. The last plastic contained held thick slices of a white, spicy cracked-pepper cheese. Finally, Donovan pulled out a loaf of bread with a crusty brown exterior and a soft white center… I held it under my nose, inhaling the rich aroma, as the steam pouring off the top warmed my face. He handed me half the loaf of bread. </i><br /><br />I shortened it for the sake of saving brain cells and eye sights but translation: Talia likes her food. <br /><br />Okay, since I’ve pointed out what I disliked about this book, I will point out what I did like about this book because overall, it wasn’t that bad. I really like the team dynamic with Talia, Henri, and Erik. I just wished we could have seen more of that. I wanted more missions, so we could see them work together and grow, but unfortunately, the plot took a backseat to the romance in this book which is a shame because this book had potential. I don’t see myself recommending this, but I might go and read the next book in the series. Things started to pick up towards the end of this book, so I am curious to see where this will go. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5904413507692570810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_274684786" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/274684786" />
    <a title="Booknut" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6917862-booknut"><img alt="Booknut" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411194489p2/6917862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/274684786?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Booknut" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Booknut" href="/user/show/6917862-booknut">Booknut</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=books-i-love-dearly">books-i-love-dearly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=can-t-get-enough-of">can-t-get-enough-of</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=cliff-hanger-endings">cliff-hanger-endings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer274684786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer786826834040740809"><b>In a futuristic setting, life on Earth has turned upside down.</b><br/><br/>Due to the Great Contamination - and the leaking of nuclear waste resulting in nuclear contamination - a generation of children with abnormalities are brought into the world. Some, though, are slightly weirder than others. <br/><br/><b>They are the Talented.</b><br/><br/>Whether Morphers, Light Manipulators or Telekinetics, these kids are taught to hone their abilities and make use of them under the protective eye of the government. To use their Talents for goo</span>
  <span id="freeText786826834040740809" style="display:none"><b>In a futuristic setting, life on Earth has turned upside down.</b><br /><br />Due to the Great Contamination - and the leaking of nuclear waste resulting in nuclear contamination - a generation of children with abnormalities are brought into the world. Some, though, are slightly weirder than others. <br /><br /><b>They are the Talented.</b><br /><br />Whether Morphers, Light Manipulators or Telekinetics, these kids are taught to hone their abilities and make use of them under the protective eye of the government. To use their Talents for good. <br /><br /><b>But all Talia wants is revenge.</b><br /><br />Talia joins the Hunters, in the hopes of one day killing Ian Crane - the man who had her parents killed before her eyes. But she has a lot to learn. With help from Hunters Erik and Henri she trains to become what she believes will help ease the pain inside. <br /><br />A thousand question run through her head: Who is she really hurting? Is Donovan, her life-long friend, her true love? Or is Erik, her right hand man? Is revenge a dish best served cold? And most importantly, is the government really protecting the Talented...or is there something sinister occurring behind the smiling facades? <br /><br /><b>A action-packed H.I.V.E-like adventure, about a group of teenagers who aren't afraid to embrace their fears and fight for what they believe.</b><br /><br /><br /><u>My Notes:</u><br /><br />First things first - I loved it!<br /><br />The whole idea was so vividly put to paper, that I could immediately see it in my mind - all thoroughly explained so as to immerse the reader in this world so like our own and yet, so different. Talia's emotions are yours; her pain your pain, her loss yours. She never scrambles her words, and funnily enough - unlike most heroines - is the first to admit to be either too clingy, or too afraid. She sees her faults and it is that which makes her all the more real.<br /><br />The other characters are a joy to read: <br /><br />Erik (whom I nickname the Fire Truck 'cause his looks could set the building on fire, lol) is sarcastic, strong, has that relaxed graceful way of doing everything - like he was born to be brilliant - and yet underneath all the bravado is a really sweet and concerned guy, who's just afraid to be rejected. <br /><br />Henri's basically like Talia's stand-in Dad - there with all the curfew reminders, no-boys-allowed rules and of course the heart-felt advice that makes him such a loveable character. <br /><br />Donovan...well. Hmph. You'll see, that's all I'm saying for now. I like him so much better BEFORE he got so...clingy. NOT a good boyfriend trait. <br /><br />Penny's fantastic. She reminds me of Penny from Hairspray mixed with a really nail-polish happy, chirpy BFF of any typical teenage girl. <br /><br />I especially love Talia, for no better reason other than she's part Italian and I love Italy and Italian food. *laughs* Jokes!!! I love her because she has a moral compass and a sense of struggle; she's not afraid to give it all she's got and she knows how to prioritise.<br /><br />(Example: Which is more important...boy troubles? Or the infiltration mission coming up? Hmm...take a guess, anyone?!)<br />(BTW - she picks the mission, for all you smarty-pants' out there!)<br /><br />I want to just thank Sophie herself for introducing me to her lovely and engaging novel - the sequel to which, Caged, will be released very soon to my excitement! </span>
  <a data-text-id="786826834040740809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3033606823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3033606823" />
    <a title="NAT.orious reads ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54624224-nat-orious-reads"><img alt="NAT.orious reads ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606165351p2/54624224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3033606823?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NAT.orious reads ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NAT.orious reads ☾" href="/user/show/54624224-nat-orious-reads">NAT.orious reads ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/35385740-talented">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54624224-nat-orious-reads?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3033606823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15399301890322131007"><u>
  <b>4 ★★★★✩, that are way more special than MC thinks she is</b>
</u><br/><i>
  <blockquote>
<b>This book is for you if… </b> the descirption "science-fiction x young adult crossover a la x-men meets divergent" sounds tempting enough to give this a try. The heroine is exhausting, though, but it was worth it in my opinion.</blockquote>
</i><br/><b>⤐ <i>Overall.</i></b><br/>A visual description of me after finishing this book:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1573121111ra/28414950.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1573121145ra/28414953.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I honestly didn't think <i>Talented</i> would manage to suck me in quite as much as it did. I checked out many reviews before starting the first audiobook a</span>
  <span id="freeText15399301890322131007" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>4 ★★★★✩, that are way more special than MC thinks she is</b>
</u><br><i>
  <blockquote>
<b>This book is for you if… </b> the descirption "science-fiction x young adult crossover a la x-men meets divergent" sounds tempting enough to give this a try. The heroine is exhausting, though, but it was worth it in my opinion.</blockquote>
</i><br><b>⤐ <i>Overall.</i></b><br>A visual description of me after finishing this book:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1573121111ra/28414950.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1573121145ra/28414953.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I honestly didn't think <i>Talented</i> would manage to suck me in quite as much as it did. I checked out many reviews before starting the first audiobook and although I still agree with some of the criticism brought up I was positively surprised how eager I was to continue the story. And the ending, my <i>goodness</i> the ending. I was just ... well, the gifs above say express my reaction pretty clearly.<br><br>Overall, the bookverse and the plot were well designed. I sometimes missed a clearer direction of where the plot is heading. Sometimes I had the suspicion the authors couldn't decide on the ratio of romance and sci-fi, which I thought especially annoying considering the MC is supposed to be an assassin in training. How much time for lovers do these trainees have? Sure, they're teenagers and need time to develop - <i>yadda yadda yadda</i>.They're about to become ruthless killers so there's really no point exploring this argument.<br><br>Since I'm already nagging, I'd like to continue. The MC was really exhausting. Repeatedly, from the beginning on, we learn that she considers herself an outsider with <i>super duper</i> special skills: she's the almighty mind-manipulator, y'all, behold. It's true that her circumstances did alienate her a bit from her fellow trainees but, honestly, if you spend all your free time with your significant other and don't even try to socialise ... I don't know what to tell ya. In combination with the ongoing communication of "specialness", I can understand why many readers gave up. I guess I blended that out eventually since I was lucky enough to listen to the audiobook.<br><br><blockquote>
<b>⤐ </b>There's one review I read that got me really pissed of. The author of said review described Talia as a tease because there were moments in the book where she got very intimate with her boyfriend but then realized she wasn't ready to have sex with him yet and thereby refused to do so. Lemme tell you something, <i>missy</i>. Even if a person were stark naked and rubbing themselves all over their partner(s), genitals up front, that person still has the right to change their mind - at any point. Nobody is obligated to have sex with anyone, <i>no. matter. what</i>. Everything else is called sexual assault and rape.</blockquote><br><br>Apart from that, I really really liked <i>Talented</i>. I enjoyed the romance-part, I thought it was captivating, just like the rest of the story. The MC's personal quest was woven in perfectly with the rest of the plot. The side characters were interesting and diverse and I'm really happy I can dive right into the sequel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35385631.Caged__Talented_Saga___2_" title="Caged (Talented Saga, #2) by Sophie Davis" rel="nofollow noopener">Caged</a>.<br><br><b>⤐ <i>What’s happening.</i></b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘TOXIC is an agency within the government that utilizes each child's unique ability in the most advantageous way.’</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Working for them obviously can't be fun. After her family is slaughtered, Natalia joins fellow talented teenagers at MacDonough to train to become a ruthless assassins, instrumentalised by TOXIC to fight the coalition that is hell-bent on destroying the talented society (or something along those lines, don't nail me on it). Not only she, but her adoptive family are grooming her to become the killer she needs to be in order to avenge her family's death. She is determined and focused but will it be enough to not only get her through her first missions, but also the troubles love can cause?<br><blockquote>
<b>Con:</b><br>⇢ <i>assassin-trainee schedule is rough</i><br>⇢ <i>family drama still traumatising</i><br>⇢ <i>new teammate is agonisingly interesting</i><br><b>Pro:</b><br>⇢ <i>finally new friends</i><br>⇢ <i>squat solidarity is A+</i><br>⇢ <i>new teammate is agonisingly interesting</i>
</blockquote><br>_____________________<br><b>
  <i> Writing quality + easy of reading</i>
</b> = 3.5*<br><br><b>
  <i>pace</i>
</b> = 3.5*<br><br><b>
  <i>plot/story in general</i>
</b> = 4*<br><br><b>
  <i>plot development</i>
</b> = 4*<br><br><b>
  <i>characters</i>
</b> = 5*<br><br><b>
  <i>enjoyability</i>
</b> = 4.5*<br><br><b>
  <i>insightfulness</i>
</b> = 3*<br>_____________________<br><i>Many thanks to the author pair Sophie Davis, who provided me with an eArc in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>

<div id="review_1019782112" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1019782112" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1019782112?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=arc-netgalley">arc-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=it-aint-easy-bein-cheesy">it-aint-easy-bein-cheesy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1019782112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2576480070195086712"><b>*2.5 Stars*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>**ARC provided by Netgalley in exchange for an honest review**</i>
</b><br/><br/>So...I was really excited about this one. I got it on my Ipad and immediately put it in front of other ARCs to read...but it just didn't work for me. It didn't seem to be bad at first, and as a whole, the story actually was pretty well thought out and fun. But as the dialogue started to drag and I began to lose interest (rather quickly), I started to realize that perhaps this was not A) What I was in the mood for and B)</span>
  <span id="freeText2576480070195086712" style="display:none"><b>*2.5 Stars*</b><br><br><b>
  <i>**ARC provided by Netgalley in exchange for an honest review**</i>
</b><br><br>So...I was really excited about this one. I got it on my Ipad and immediately put it in front of other ARCs to read...but it just didn't work for me. It didn't seem to be bad at first, and as a whole, the story actually was pretty well thought out and fun. But as the dialogue started to drag and I began to lose interest (rather quickly), I started to realize that perhaps this was not A) What I was in the mood for and B) At all what I expected it to be. But, as I said before, I think the story as a whole had a lot of potential and this leads me to believe that this is, in fact, my perception of the story and that many people will love it.<br><br>Talia wants revenge on the man who killed her family-Ian Crane. She has a talent to both open the mind of others and open <i>her</i> mind in return. She is dating Donovan, the head of the Academy she will be attending's son. I loved their little bubble they hung out in at first, but as the story started to expand and the cute little moments became repetitive, I began losing interest. It was adorable when they were together, sure, but it wasn't altogether gripping paired with the story as a whole. It would say that Talia and her team were going out to train and then all of a sudden the next night would be there in a flash, or maybe I had began to zone out so frequently that I didn't realize. I just don't like when scenes aren't played out for me and I can't become immersed in the world, and I felt this happened more than once with this one.<br><br>There was also an extra love interest, Erik, who was her right hand man and teammate. Now, I did love their scenes together and I even still loved Donovan. This book made me want more, but also had me backing away. At the moment, I can't seem to find a reason to continue because I was so put off by the cheesy dialogue between Penny and Talia, the cliched moments when Donovan got jealous (that scene could have been epic-I love jealous scenes), and altogether my lack of love for the story, but, I really see myself coming back and attempting a re read in the future because this book/series holds so much promise. By the time the action and peril got to the story, I felt like I didn't care and it was too late...but maybe next time I can find the love I didn't have this time and fully immerse myself into their world.<br><br>It didn't work out for me this time, but next time I hope to be able to appreciate the action brought forth from this story and hopefully be able to love what this author has created. It is loved by countless others and I hope to join them in that love some day. But, for now, I will put this series down and take a breather.<br><br><i>For more of my reviews visit<br><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img height="240" width="385" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407869528i/10772466._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2576480070195086712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText894952866390152498" style="display:none"><b>OVERALL RATING: 4 STARS</b><br><br><b>SUMMARY</b>.The world that the story takes place was affected by Great Contamination over a hundred years before she was born. It started with natural disasters that destroyed many small cities and devastated large industrial nations. After the disaster the world has been contaminated from nuclear reactors that were buried deep in the Earth’s surface and started to leak. The eco-system was destroyed and there were come consequences. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Horses were born with horns, fish with three eyes and even two headed pigs were reported… Leaves began to glow at night, and the bark on trees grew a fuzzy coating, stinging anything that touched it</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Because of the contamination, the first generation of children was born with unnatural colored eyes and had some amazing gifts that nobody had. Morphing, Mind Manipulation, super-computer-like brain, and many more. Some people were trying to hide that their children had talents and that’s how the nation was broken into two different countries which caused a war.<br><br>When Natalia Lyons was a little girl, she witnessed her parents being murdered right in front of her. The only thing that saved her was her talents which killed all of the men. After years of training in special school for Talents, she was finally getting ready to be a Hunter, cold-blooded Operative who played a big role in the war between two countries. But aside from wanted to kill the men who took the lives of her parents, (who was actually running the riot), she wanted to feel normal and be just like a regular teenage girl. That’s why she was confused when her team partner <br>turned out to be a super hot and irresistible guy named Erik because she already had a boyfriend. <br><br><u>My Castings</u><br><br><a href="http://s1358.photobucket.com/user/bebeboss666/media/Review/Picture1_zps0bc8ab8e.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413527i/814329._SX540_.png" alt=" photo Picture1_zps0bc8ab8e.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Natalia.</b> Okay so I have to admit, she is pretty badass. There is some moments in the book that I just want to slap her because she’s being super annoying. She’s also very VERY clingy. Like when she tells the guys to stay with her, author adds: “I know I sounded desperate, but I didn’t care”.  That made me pull my hair out because I swear, the same sentence was repeated at least 3 times in the book. But she is tough, controlled, and bad ass. At the end I learned to love her. <br><br><b>Donovan.</b> The son of the main guy who runs the country and the TOXIC. At first I loved everything about him but when he <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[cheated on Natalia with a bunch of girls <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I just wanted to cut his heart out. How dare he??? I’m so glad that Natalia did what she did in the book. <br><br><b>Erik.</b> Ohhhhhhhh I want him now!! He is the player-type kin d of guy but he can also be very sweet when he wants to. I really just wanted to kiss the pages because it sounded so hot. –drool-<br><br><b>THOUGHTS</b>. I do have to say that the author could have made the beginning way better. For the first three chapters there was no explanation whatsoever and it felt like you just walked in in the middle of a joke. LIKE WTFFFFF?? But then after the author starts explaining the story and you’re like: “Ohhh yea, that actually sounds like it was worth the $0 that it costs me”. But by the end of the book I couldn’t stop reading it because it was so intense. The ending was so unfair because I really wanna know what happens to Natalia now and if she’s going to survive. But I LOOOVEd the book. <br>Grrrrrrrrrrr it’s so hard not to give out spoilers :/</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_556707559" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/556707559" />
    <a title="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit"><img alt="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372018610p2/3854740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/556707559?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" href="/user/show/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit">Christina (Ensconced in Lit)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit?shelf=author-request">author-request</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer556707559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12201757856973082705">I was given this book by the author in exchange for an honest review. I give this book 2.5 stars.<br/><br/>Talented by Sophie Davis is a Paranormal/dystopian YA of sorts that stars Talia, a girl with the Talent of telekinesis and telepathy, who has been recruited to become a Hunter. This will allow her to avenge the death of her parents by the nebulous organization, Toxic. At the same time, she has a bit of a romantic conundrum where she has a long time relationship with Donovan but is attracted to her te</span>
  <span id="freeText12201757856973082705" style="display:none">I was given this book by the author in exchange for an honest review. I give this book 2.5 stars.<br /><br />Talented by Sophie Davis is a Paranormal/dystopian YA of sorts that stars Talia, a girl with the Talent of telekinesis and telepathy, who has been recruited to become a Hunter. This will allow her to avenge the death of her parents by the nebulous organization, Toxic. At the same time, she has a bit of a romantic conundrum where she has a long time relationship with Donovan but is attracted to her teammate, Erik. Can Talia find the strength and bravery to avenge her parents' death?<br /><br />What I liked: actually, I was pretty drawn in from 70% of the book to almost the end. Talia has become a bit stronger and likeable of a character, and we get to see some cool stuff she trains with. On top of that, we see a lot more of Erik and Henri, who are probably the most likeable characters in the book. The background of the story could have been cooler with a few tweaks.<br /><br />What I had trouble with. This section will have some minor spoilers, which will not give away plot points but will discuss issues I had in the later part of the book.<br />1. Talia whines. A LOT. You probably don't want to use the word "whine" to describe a protagonist that we are supposed to like.<br />2. Science in books is very important to me. Even if it's "made up," it has to make sense within the constructs of the book. The whole gene mutation bit is not explained enough. On top of that, there is no such thing as a "hangover shot" that will rehydrate someone. You can give IV fluids to rehydrate someone with vitamins. If this is a new invention for the future, this needs to be explained.<br />3. The love triangle. Donovan is not likeable at all. Either he needs to be more likeable, or his role needs to be reduced (because of him, I almost put down the book before I finished it), or his role needs to be explained in THIS book, not the next. Also, Talia gets more and more annoying when we are talking about her love life.<br />4. The evil corporation and "bad guy." This whole side plot, which actually only takes front and center in the end, should have been talked about throughout the book. What should have happened is we should have seen a lot more angst in Talia about her parents and this "bad guy" that has ruined it. Instead, we get a description of the dude 70% in?! <br />5. There is a handwritten letter that plays an important part and reveals a TON of secrets. WHAT?! Why is there a handwritten letter in the first place with people with great technology and telepathy?! Just tell your secrets in your head!<br />6. Why would every country let their Talented all go to the US? That makes not sense to me-- every country would want to hoard these powerful people to safeguard its own interests. To get a much more brilliant take on this scenario-- read the Ender's Shadow trilogy.<br /><br />Overall, ideas had promise, but my experience of this book got bogged down in issue after issue that never got resolved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12201757856973082705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer341357512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18083295061153678268">Talia was part of a happy, loving family. Their family travels to do research on the effects the nuclear meltdown had on world’s population. Many people were born with unique powers, after the nuclear disaster, these powers are referred to as talents. Conflicts and revolutions started over these talented individuals. It seems that power is in controlling the powerful. Her family, unfortunately, was deemed a threat in this conflict. A team is sent out to eliminate them, Talia does survives but on</span>
  <span id="freeText18083295061153678268" style="display:none">Talia was part of a happy, loving family. Their family travels to do research on the effects the nuclear meltdown had on world’s population. Many people were born with unique powers, after the nuclear disaster, these powers are referred to as talents. Conflicts and revolutions started over these talented individuals. It seems that power is in controlling the powerful. Her family, unfortunately, was deemed a threat in this conflict. A team is sent out to eliminate them, Talia does survives but only after she witnesses the brutal murder of her parents. She declares to take revenge on the man she’s been told ordered the hit. She is sent to a special school that trains the talented, Talia is telekinetic. After graduating she applies to become a hunter. In hunter training, Talia is molded into a weapon of war. Talia must face betrayal, love, and ultimately herself (does she really have what it takes to become a killer). <br /><br />I absolutely loved Talented. This book is packed full of fresh and stunning imagery of this dystophian world…you feel like you right there. The characters are wonderful. Talia is so real, you feel for everything she goes through as if she is your best friend. The tension between Talia, Donavon and Erik, is simply fantastic! I’m going to go click Caged right now, because this book left me with the bereft feeling of needing more NOW! <br /><br />This copy of Talented was given to me by Goodreads Making Connections Group and Sophie Davis in exchange for an honest review.</span>

<div id="review_890305146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/890305146" />
    <a title="Abbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10194401-abbie"><img alt="Abbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374780271p2/10194401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/890305146?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abbie" href="/user/show/10194401-abbie">Abbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer890305146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6988987584469705683"><b>Actual rating - 1.5</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13466202.Talented__Talented_Saga___1_' title='Talented (Talented Saga, #1) by Sophie Davis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Talented</a> was a really hard book to get through.<br/>I put it down at 75% because i couldn't take any more.<br/>I had to force myself to finish it 8 hours later, and it took chocolate to make it tolerable. <br/><br/>I was bored from the first chapter.<br/>Even when there was a bit of action, i was still bored. <br/><br/>The characters were rubbish.<br/>I didn't like any of them, but Talia was defiantly the one i liked least.<br/><br/>Overall, rubbish.</span>

<div id="review_836205101" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/836205101" />
    <a title="Koeur" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21736404-koeur"><img alt="Koeur" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378529798p2/21736404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/836205101?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Koeur" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Koeur" href="/user/show/21736404-koeur">Koeur</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer836205101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1512423320404163251"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://koeur.wordpress.com/2014/01/28/review-talented-1-by-sophie-davis/'>http://koeur.wordpress.com/2014/01/28...</a><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>Publisher: Indie Linked<br/> Publishing Date: January 2014<br/> ISBN: 9781618429940<br/> Genre: Fantasy<br/> Rating: 1.2/5.0<br/><br/>Publisher Description: If Sookie and 007 had a love child with a yearning for vengeance, her story would be TALENTED.<br/><br/>Review: Wow, Sookie huh? That should create of flood of readership. This reads more like if two retarded baboons had a manifestation of frenetic copulation their story would be TALENTED…. The cover art looks like a magicians assistant in a</span>
  <span id="freeText1512423320404163251" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://koeur.wordpress.com/2014/01/28/review-talented-1-by-sophie-davis/">http://koeur.wordpress.com/2014/01/28...</a><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Publisher: Indie Linked<br /> Publishing Date: January 2014<br /> ISBN: 9781618429940<br /> Genre: Fantasy<br /> Rating: 1.2/5.0<br /><br />Publisher Description: If Sookie and 007 had a love child with a yearning for vengeance, her story would be TALENTED.<br /><br />Review: Wow, Sookie huh? That should create of flood of readership. This reads more like if two retarded baboons had a manifestation of frenetic copulation their story would be TALENTED…. The cover art looks like a magicians assistant in a stage performance.<br /><br />The first 30% of this novel is a lengthy backstory told within the bounds of LUV between Donavan and Talia. He is so ready for sex and she is teasing him beyond belief. She allows him to undress her to her undies and gets him all worked up only to back out. This is a constant theme throughout the novel. Talia is really Donavan’s step-sister who came to live with them when her parents were killed at a very young age. So its kind of creepy that they are kissing and fondling when in reality they should be repelled by those actions. The “It’s like kissing your sister” line.<br /><br />So there were these underground nuclear reactors worldwide that melted down, no one could fix it then all of a sudden children were born with various abilities. No one can link any genetic mutation to the environmental crisis and trees are growing fur and dogs have feathers. So blah, blah, blah, and Talia’s’ parents are killed by rebels who hate Talents but Talia goes apeshit and kills Ten rebel operatives with her mind during a fit of rage/mourning. Why? Because she is oh so freakin’ speshul, that’s why. And don’t you forget it or Talia will telepathikinesis yur ass straight back to Texas/Nevada/Utah/Idaho/Arizona (all the bad states) for fucks sake. They have hormone addled teenagers performing deep covert ops to retrieve “information” from the coalition. Inter-twined within this non-existent story-line is this sordid love triangle. <br /><br />Talia is a whiney, dick teasing asshat with the morals of a pigeon. She invokes love triangles amidst her burgeoning desires to screw anything male and hairy. Her failsafe response to everything are these mini-tantrums where indignant behavior is tantamount to righteousness. And then the coin lands on tails and we have clingy, whiney-baby Talia who wuvs her man and needs his stwong awrms awound her. Fug. There is this lengthy teen angst emotive spew page after page after page. Talia finds Donavan in the arms of some “blonde slut” bimbo. Well duh. What do you expect? But never fear, she has a backup plan that involves Mr. Turquoise eyes/ripply muscles Erik because she has never felt a kiss like that that has effected her so profoundly. Talia wastes no time teasing Erik by performing the same undie ritual as she did with Donavon. <br /><br />The writing utilizes the tried and true overuse of certain words to help describe scenes and situations. About halfway through this disaster, I counted the word “Actually” 84 times as it was used pretty repetitively. Other words used consistently to the determinant of the novel were; “thankfully”, “gratefully”, “defensively”, “grudgingly” “mentally”, “grumbled”, “regretfully”, “carefully”, “scowl”, “pointedly”, “dryly”, “tentatively”, “mumbled x30″ and “growled”. <br /><br />Character development revolves around an extremely ego-centric and insecure main character. Rather than cheer for her, you end up loathing her actions that are based within the bounds of her little mind. There is no real giving of herself. Every decision she makes is predicated on what’s best for her. She seems to reflect the current state of consciousness in most people, so the author got that right at least. This novel needed to be edited way down in terms of dialogue and the story-line compressed. Talia needs to stand on her own as a tough operative in a world of espionage. She can be tough yet tender not clingy, whiney and self-absorbed. The men in her life should be minor interests for the sake of believability. This is slated to be an ongoing series. The author needs to consider getting professional editing services prior to publishing. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1512423320404163251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3294059927197331584">I received this book free from the author in exchange for an honest review.<br/>I loved Talented! I enjoyed the whole storyline, the idea of the Talented and how they ended up where they are now and how they were "created". I felt like it was a pretty unique background story. I also liked reading about the types of Talented and what their abilities are. I liked the kind of love triangle that was going on and I loved all of the sexual tension. Talented flowed really smoothly and it made for a quick en</span>
  <span id="freeText3294059927197331584" style="display:none">I received this book free from the author in exchange for an honest review.<br />I loved Talented! I enjoyed the whole storyline, the idea of the Talented and how they ended up where they are now and how they were "created". I felt like it was a pretty unique background story. I also liked reading about the types of Talented and what their abilities are. I liked the kind of love triangle that was going on and I loved all of the sexual tension. Talented flowed really smoothly and it made for a quick entertaining read. By the end of the book, i really want to grab book two and get started.<br />I loved most of these characters, if you have read the book you know what I mean. Talia was a great heroine to read about. She had overcame a lot in her young life. She always pulled out on top and was the bigger person. I'm hoping now that she can somewhat settle down and be happy. I want to read all about it. I really like Erik but I wish that he would have told Talia earlier about scummy scumbag. I also enjoyed how Erik and Talia would bicker back and forth and the sexual tension, oh my! I also found Henri to be a fun character and I hope that he gets a spin off.<br />Overall, I loved this book and I can't wait to carry on with the series and see where the characters end up. I would recommend this book to paranormal readers. But I would suggest having book two beside you to pick up when you finish book one.<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer562520634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12873008572243539056">A nuclear disaster causes the Great Contamination and special abilities in the children. Called, “Talents,” they are often feared for the abilities they possess. When young Talia’s parents are murdered while investigating the nuclear fallout, she is taken in by one the heads of an elite government unit that trains the talents, for Sophie, her abilities make her an excellent “hunter.” We are invited to follow Talia’s life as she learns to maneuver the ins and outs of training, life as a talent an</span>
  <span id="freeText12873008572243539056" style="display:none">A nuclear disaster causes the Great Contamination and special abilities in the children. Called, “Talents,” they are often feared for the abilities they possess. When young Talia’s parents are murdered while investigating the nuclear fallout, she is taken in by one the heads of an elite government unit that trains the talents, for Sophie, her abilities make her an excellent “hunter.” We are invited to follow Talia’s life as she learns to maneuver the ins and outs of training, life as a talent and possibly falling in love with her best friend, who may not be the best choice as boyfriend material. When she should be concentrating on being trained as a formidable assassin, she gets distracted by a brash and boldly handsome talent that even as he is needling her, gets under her skin and starts chipping away at her heart. Take a ride on this adventurous journey in this dystopian world where being a teen, alone, out for revenge for her parents’ murders is only part of the drama in Talia’s life, after all, she has to contend with being a talent and having feelings for more than one boy.<br><br>This is not my first time reading <b>Talented</b> by Sophie Davis, but for whatever reason, I enjoyed this so much more the second time around. Was it timing? Paying more attention to the talents of the author? Truly feeling the character’s as they come alive in a fantasy world of the near future? Wonderful emotion-filled drama, adventure and pure teen exuberance with well-developed characters, to boot!!<br><br>I received an ARC of the re—release of <b>Talented</b> from Indie Inked in exchange for my honest review.<br><br>Re-Publication Date: January 14, 2014<br>Publisher: Indie Inked<br>ISBN: 9781618429940<br>Genre: YA/Teen Paranormal Romance | Sci-fi<br>Number of Pages: 378<br>Available from: <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Talented-Saga-1-Sophie-Davis-ebook/dp/B0076Y7ON4/ref=sr_1_1?s=digital-text&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1396643109&amp;sr=1-1&amp;keywords=talented" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> | <a href="http://www.barnesandnoble.com/w/talented-sophie-davis/1108057717?ean=2940044269002" rel="nofollow noopener">Barnes &amp; Noble </a><br><br><a href="http://tometender.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396145073i/9095116._SX540_.jpg" height="241" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>My Original review 2012<br>The story had great character development. I loved Erik. His character was so flawed, yet he had a lot of good going on, too. Talia was stronger than she knew, tough, yet vulnerable. Definitely a great read about a dystopian society, teen angst, having to live larger than life through all of the pressures. July 1, 2012</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696923287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16097416504334699622">I received this book in exchange for an honest review via Lovers of Paranormal Group! :)<br/><br/>I love Natalia! She is a very relatable character. <br/>The entire cast is well thought out and described well too. <br/>You really get pulled into Hunter's Village. <br/>I was happy, sad, mad and hurt right along with Talia. My fingernails suffered on her missions! <br/>I love the plot and the twists as well. I cannot wait to read Caged!<br/>Her mission with Henri and Erik was awesome!<br/> Especially what Erik does for her... Just amazi</span>
  <span id="freeText16097416504334699622" style="display:none">I received this book in exchange for an honest review via Lovers of Paranormal Group! :)<br /><br />I love Natalia! She is a very relatable character. <br />The entire cast is well thought out and described well too. <br />You really get pulled into Hunter's Village. <br />I was happy, sad, mad and hurt right along with Talia. My fingernails suffered on her missions! <br />I love the plot and the twists as well. I cannot wait to read Caged!<br />Her mission with Henri and Erik was awesome!<br /> Especially what Erik does for her... Just amazing!<br />Things go bad and good and crazy and it was a thrill to read!<br /><br />And oh.... my gawd! Her solo mission was intense!!! I was shaking my leg uncontrollably and biting my nails until the last page! And wow! I am so glad I have Caged to read now!!<br /><br /><br />Definitely recommend this series!<br /><br /><br />★★★★★★★★★★★★★<br />SPOILER ALERT!!!!<br />IF YOU CLICK THE LINK TO SHOW SPOILERS YOU WILL INDEED SPOIL THE STORY!!! <br />IF YOU HAVE NOT READ THIS BOOK AND DO NOT WANT IT SPOILED THEN DO NOT CLICK IT!!!<br />Unless of course you are one of the brave few who wants to know before you read it! Then by all means click away!<br />That is all..... carry on.....<br />★★★★★★★★★★★★★★<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[text&gt;<br /><br /><br />Talia is in distress when we find her. She's woken up by blaring sirens and even worse she's alone. She goes outside barefoot in her p.j.'s! Soon it all becomes clear when bombs start exploding around them that turn out to be colored water then paint for the finale. <br />Donavon who is apparently close to her and not in proximity is controlling the bombs. <br />She gets upset and goes back to bed but he gets her back out for the finale. <br />Welcoming the Pledges to the Hunters Village where they train to be Hunters.<br />She's been at McDonough's School for the Talented for seven years and has been waiting for that moment. <br />She was taken in by Mac the schools owner when her parents were murdered by Ian Crane or The Coalition. TOXIC is who Talia is working for and training is her top priority. Fueled by revenge for her parents deaths she keeps to herself.<br /><br />Later on in life she became his son Donavon's girlfriend. He's at Hunter's Village too and they spend as much time as possible together. <br />Mac gives Talia permission to go into the city with Henri and Erik her teammates. They celebrate and she has fun. <br />Donavon is starting to worry me when he acts weird when he's the one going into the city at night. That same night she meets Penny and they become fast friends.<br />Him and Talia have been apart since he had moved to Hunter's Village before her. She wanted to spend every second with him. He was starting to seem shady to me.<br /><br />Talia gets her first mission and she's psyched. She has been training for this. She's the three way communication for them with her powerful mental abilities.<br />She trains hard and things are going great till her boyfriend accuses her of liking Erik. He eventually comes with apologies and she forgives him.<br /><br />The mission is on and she saved Erik but got stabbed in the process. They got what they came for and it was time to go. They had to get Talia back to safety to pull out the knife. Henri takes care of her and I cried while Erik filtered out her pain and took it for her. That was the most beautiful thing ever! <br />She has some healing to do but she also has some thinking to do. She felt something when Erik took her pain and it confused her. Erik was ready to talk but Talk wasn't. Donavon is back from a mission and him and Talia spend some time together and then he says he is going into town and it gets suspicious to me. <br />Erik and Henri come back from a night in D.C. and Erik's cheek is cut. Talia tries to find out what happened but Erik is upset with her but she doesn't know why. <br />She goes to find a drunk Donovan and he's beat up. She thinks they fought over her. Silly girl! Donavon sticks to her like glue until she gets any break from him to go on missions. Can you say shady! She's worried about being alone with Erik, afraid of what she had felt before. Nothing happens and she's relieved. The three missions go smoothly and they are back at headquarters ahead of time and all Talk wants to do is see Donavon. She heads straight to his cabin and pauses.... I knew what would happen but I was still peeved when she caught him in bed with a nondescript blonde. Talia get unequivocally mad! As a woman she did what any scorned woman wishes she could do in that situation! Instant suffrage for Donavon. I guiltily enjoyed every second of her 'blow up'. I applauded her on it! I'm happy that Donavon was found out. On the other hand I hate to see Talia getting her heart ripped out. But I think she'll be better off without him as her boyfriend. They've known each other so long I don't see it being the absolute end. But we shall see! <br />She grieves her love for Donavon. Can't blame her. It would truly suck to be her at that moment. <br /><br /><i> "I felt something inside of me freeze and then shatter into a million pieces. My heart." </i><br /><br />Gut wrenching! <br /><br />So Talia wakes Erik's there explain what he knows then Mac comes by and tells her he wants her to focus on training and missions and he's moving her team to the apartments.<br />Talk does just that. They go on mission after mission for a while successful the whole way. Erik and Tal get closer but not romantic. She gets her first Kill mission and the nervous vibe is palpable. <br />Things go good but in the end she doesn't take the target out herself. The mission is a success but she's not happy she didn't do it herself.<br />Talia gets drunk on Festivis night and her and Erik get cozy...She's all go in her tipsy state but Erik's a gentlemen and puts on the brakes.<br />Mind reading backfires when it comes to intimate moments for Talia. She hemorrhages thoughts of life with Donavon. He's the only love she's ever known. I just think it's too much for Erik.<br /><br />Avoiding the awkwardness she starts training hard core and she is doing great!<br />This is it. Ian Crane the man synonymous with the death of her parents and her solo graduate determining mission is his headquarters and on the dlo, him.<br />Erik and her have a great moment but its short. Back to business. As she prepares for her solo mission Erik spends time with her after the team goes home for the night. They are definitely getting closer and closer.<br />Talia asks him about his past and he says she's not ready to hear it. She's confused. It's her celebration dinner and she gets torre up on some no hang over stuff and her and Erik go back to her apartment but the internal comparisons between Donavon and Erik are driving Erik crazy and he's basically has enough. He says she's drunk and should just go to sleep but she insists to know and he tells her and it doesn't end well. She cries herself to sleep and it's solo mission time the next morning. <br />She goes on her mission and all goes well till she goes head to head with Ian Crane himself...... <br />I know I spoiled alot but the end you have to see for yourself and I left alot out!<br /><br />I will say I was mortified for both Erik and Talia at who found the letter meant for Talia. I hope he does the right thing! Grrr.<br /><br />I recommend this book for sure!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6204112095896308344">Ebook: Talented<br/>Author: Sophie Davis<br/>Fiction, Paranormal,<br/>This review may contain spoilers<br/>Summary: When Talia Lyons was just a child, her parents were murdered before her eyes. Offered a choice between accepting their fate and exacting revenge, Talia trains to become one of the country’s deadliest assassins in order to kill the man responsible for their deaths: Ian Crane. Luckily, Talia was born with a gift- the ability to read and influence the minds of others. At sixteen, Talia is poised to gradu</span>
  <span id="freeText6204112095896308344" style="display:none">Ebook: Talented<br />Author: Sophie Davis<br />Fiction, Paranormal,<br />This review may contain spoilers<br />Summary: When Talia Lyons was just a child, her parents were murdered before her eyes. Offered a choice between accepting their fate and exacting revenge, Talia trains to become one of the country’s deadliest assassins in order to kill the man responsible for their deaths: Ian Crane. Luckily, Talia was born with a gift- the ability to read and influence the minds of others. At sixteen, Talia is poised to graduate from the McDonough School for the Talented, where she learned to control her abilities. Now there is only one obstacle standing between her and the retribution she craves... Talia herself.<br />Her greatest asset may also be her undoing; while a formidable weapon in the field, Talia’s talents prevent her from both shutting off the mental connection she shares with her questionable boyfriend and blocking out the thoughts of a beguiling fellow recruit. But Talia can’t afford to have the feelings and distractions of a normal teenage girl, when her life is far from normal.<br />She must regain the single-minded determination that has brought her this far, or it may cost Talia her life when she finally faces Crane. And even after being molded in to a weapon of war, she’ll still have to find the strength it takes to pull the trigger.<br />If James Bond and Sookie Stackhouse had a love child with a yearning for vengeance, her story would be TALENTED: an adventure about powerful teenagers who aren’t afraid to embrace their fears and fight for what they believe in.<br /><br />The Review<br />How have I not read this series, bad bad reviewer, I loved this book, Book 2 &amp; 3 are both firmly ensconced in my TBR list, Talia is such a great character, I really believed I was going through everything with her, she was so kick ass when she needed to be, but she had a soft side that really touched my heart, this book has an amazing plot line, different from anything else I have read, it will keep you on the edge of your seat, The characters are well written, full of character, there were others in the book that to me really brought the book together as a whole, I love Talia’s room mates, the fact that she has 2 males she is living with really made this book super funny in places, I would recommend this to everyone, it will have you laughing in so many places, I even cried in a couple of places, this was so well written, I felt Talia’s pain, 5/5<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9841207001985845401">**This book was given to me for an honest review**<br/><br/>Oh, wow! I'm still reeling from this phenomenal and stunning story! Seriously people I am in complete fan girl mode! Where the heck has this masterpiece been hiding?!?! <br/><br/>Omg,OMG OOOMMMMGGG!!!<br/><br/>Okay, I think I'm good now, no more fan girling!   <span id="freeText9841207001985845401" style="display:none">**This book was given to me for an honest review**<br /><br />Oh, wow! I'm still reeling from this phenomenal and stunning story! Seriously people I am in complete fan girl mode! Where the heck has this masterpiece been hiding?!?! <br /><br />Omg,OMG OOOMMMMGGG!!!<br /><br />Okay, I think I'm good now, no more fan girling! So, this is a fearsome, awe-inspiring, breath taking book. It literally has everything in it you could possibly crave. Sophie Davis paints a beautiful and tragic world, with such descriptive and poetic writing you can't help but feel the pull of the story. The characters are well rounded with normal deficiencies and amazing attributes. Truly stunning story! <br /><br />It starts off by explaining the world and how it has been turned upside-down, flipped and twisted by nuclear weapons hidden in the earth. The spread effects the whole world, the ocean, animals and eventually the people making children come to the world with deformities and amazing abilities. As time goes on these wane and drift but the "talented" remain, and are chosen to fight for the government.<br />The main character Talia, is one of the effected humans and has gifts of her own. She is an amazing talented lead character who faces so many trail and tribulations in her short life, that you wonder how she has survived. The answer is revenge. She joins the "Hunters" to avenge her past and grow her future.<br /><br />Talia is not alone in this tremendous world Sophie painted for you, she has her friends and handsome side kicks. My favorite among them is our dashing and witty heart breaker Erik, who was a huge part of why I fell so fast for 'Talented'. <br />Talia's journey with her friends Erik, Henri, Donovan and little Penelope is provocative, thrilling, funny, heart wrenching and riveting. <br /><br />This book will have you in craze, waiting to find out what happens next with the plot twist and constant adventures. I loved it and truly can't wait to dig into the series, I absolutely recommend it to everyone and anyone. But especially those of you looking for a fun read with romance, adventure, mystery and a beautiful dystopian world ready for you to join! Enjoy!<br /><br />Enjoy this book! I know I did! <br /><br />You can also find my reviews at <a href="http://heaventoearthreviews.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Heaven to Earth Reviews</a><br /> </span>

<div id="review_960109507" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/960109507" />
    <a title="Lindaisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12538079-lindaisa"><img alt="Lindaisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591500692p2/12538079.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/960109507?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindaisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindaisa" href="/user/show/12538079-lindaisa">Lindaisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13466008-talented">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer960109507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15094200629621441475">I'm going to keep this short because I have a migraine right now and the ending of this book didn't do a thing to help it. Let's just say I'm glad I got this book when it was Free on amazon.<br/><br/>This book was going to get a 3 star rating until I read that ending with what I am deeming the sorriest excuse for a <i>'cliffhanger'</i> that I've ever read in my life. <br/><br/>But I'm getting ahead of myself. From the very beginning of the book, there was something off about the writing that I couldn't pinpoint until last</span>
  <span id="freeText15094200629621441475" style="display:none">I'm going to keep this short because I have a migraine right now and the ending of this book didn't do a thing to help it. Let's just say I'm glad I got this book when it was Free on amazon.<br /><br />This book was going to get a 3 star rating until I read that ending with what I am deeming the sorriest excuse for a <i>'cliffhanger'</i> that I've ever read in my life. <br /><br />But I'm getting ahead of myself. From the very beginning of the book, there was something off about the writing that I couldn't pinpoint until last night when I started reading another book. This book isn't written like a novel. Its written like a teenage girls diary.<br /><br />25% into the book and I still didn't know what the point of the book was or what the plot was going to be because Talia, the main character and narrator, was too busy detailing her everyday life training with her team and making out with her boyfriend by the lake.<br /><br />Nothing is ever really explained in this book which was a problem for me because for the majority of the book, I'm wondering "<i>What am I reading this for...What is the purpose of everything that is going on.</i>" I can't even really tell you what Talia's Talent is. I know she can communicate telepathically. I know she can move objects with her mind and I know she can impose her will on others. But she never really uses her abilities besides to uselessly open doors that are right in front of her or to have conversations with her partners and her boyfriend. -- The only reason I feel like I didn't put this book down is because there was this silly little love triangle between Talia, one of her partners Erik, and her long time best friend and boyfriend Donovan. <br /><br />That's kind of sad to be honest though. The redeeming quality of this book for me was a love triangle...And I <b>HATE</b> love triangles. <br /><br />I'm not sure anything really happened in Talented because I'm still not clear what the point of the story is. Talia is a pledge in an agency called TOXIC who uses people with Talents to further their agenda...whatever that is. She and her teammates, Henri and Erik go on a few missions to obtain data and information from a rival agency called the Coalition that is against people with Talents. I don't really know what happened on those missions or why they needed the information they obtained because...it's never explained and no one ever talks about it.<br /><br />Besides being vaguely aware of what was going on, there was a lot of juvenile teenage stuff to keep me entertained. Talia made a friend named Penny while getting super drunk for the first time in her life at a bonfire. They got dressed up and went out to the city a few times together...<br /><br />I don't even....*sighs* I was going to give this book a 3 star rating because while I was confused about the point the entire time and while nothing was ever really explained or developed...I was entertained while reading it. I liked the tension between Erik and Talia, and I liked that Henri had a gorgeous boyfriend named Frederick. But then the ending happened and just pissed me completely off. I won't go into it because its a spoiler...I <b>GUESS.</b> But it was silly, anticlimactic and pointless. There was some information revealed about someone but that information really has no bearing and isn't a threat because said person has no intentions on doing anything about their situation. <b>POINTLESS.</b> <br /><br />I'm done...I'm not reading the next book or any of the others, that's for sure. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15094200629621441475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
